COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Submitted a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
WlL.LIAM R. MORAN, Co unty Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, on September 11 , 2001 , the United States of America was shocked by an attack within our
borders; and

3476

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 2001

WHEREAS, by Joint Resolution the Cong ress of the United States of America committed to support
increased resources in the war to eradicate terrorism; and
WHEREAS, the tragic events of September 11th caused the Federal Government and Governments
around the world to consider and increase security efforts; and
WHEREAS, the American public supports increased security in order to protect our nation, American
C itizens and others in our Country; and
WHEREAS, local Police Departments in Cook County increased the length of officer' s shifts and paid
thousands of dollars to those officers in overtime pay; and
WHEREAS, Police Officers in Cook County were patrolling around schools and religious institutions in
order to protect the people of Cook County and keep the peace; and
WHEREAS, several towns in Cook County, including Burbank, Oak Lawn, Justice, Summit and
Bridgeview, spent thousands of dollars for increased police patrols after September 11 , 200 I; and
WHEREAS, the Sheriffs Office is assisted by and assists other law enforcement agencies in and around
Cook County, w henever any assistance is needed; and
WHEREAS, the Sheriffs Office assisted several communities on th e days following September 11 ,
2001; and
WHEREAS, the Sheriff s Office's efforts to help other agencies is greatly appreciated and shows the
generosity of the Sheriffs Office and Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the
Sheriff's Office should make every effort to continue to assist law enforcement agencies of Cook County,
especially those burdened by increased overtime costs from police patrols.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commiss ioner Silvestri , moved to s uspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Moran moved that the Proposed Reso lution be approved and adopted. The motion died
for lack of a second.

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY
TERMINATION OF CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated October 18, 200 I from
MICHA ELE. LAMONT, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy
On September 25, 200 I and September 28, 200 I, Siemens/Faustech, a Joint Venture, a DD Industries,
LLC Company, (DD Industries) was notified that it was in default of Contract No. 00-53-844, a contract
for the purchase of radiology equipment for the New Cook County Hospital, ("Contract") pursuant to the
Contract's General Condition-19, Default. DD Industries has failed to remedy these defaults in a timely
fashion. The Board of Commissioners is respectfully requested to approve the recommendation to
declare the rights of DD Industries in the contract forfeited pursuant to the terms of the contract and to
terminate the contract effective immed iately.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to terminate the contract with
Siemens/Faustech, a Joint Venture, a DD Industries, LLC Company (DD Industries) pursuant to the
Contract's General Condition-19, Default. The motion carried.

Commissioners Collins, Hansen and Quigley voted "present".
Commissioners Butler, Moran and Schumann were absent.
*Note: See related item under the Executive Session, page 36 17 of this journal.
CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated October 18, 2001 from
MICHA ELE. LAMONT, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter
into a contract with General Electric Company d/b/a GE Medical Systems, Oak Brook, Illinois, for the
installation and delivery of radiology equipment for the New Cook County Hospital, and for authorization
for execution of this contract.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $57,268,836.00. Bond Issue (22000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to enter into and execute the requested contract. The motion carried.

Commissioners Collins, Hansen, Maldonado, Quigley and Sutker voted "no".
Commissioners Butler, Moran and Schumann were absent.

CAPITAL PROGRAM ITEM
Transmining a Communication from
MICHAELE. LAMONT, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy
requesting approval of Contract Modification No. 4 in the amount of $2,806,000.00 payable to
Walsh/Riteway Joint Venture, Construction Manager for the New Cook County Hospital Project. It is
res pectfully requested that this honorable body approve this request.
Thi s amount is a not-to-exceed allowance to cover replacement workers' compensation, employe r's
liabi li ty insurance and general liabi lity after November 2, 2001. These coverages were included in the
Wrap-up Program approved by this Board on November 7, 1996. Reliance Insurance Company was
placed under an Order of Liquidation by the Pennsylvania Department of Insurance on October 3, 2001.
Pursuant to the Order, a ll policies are cancelled effective November 2, 200 I.
Both the County's program manager, Partnership for Community Healthcare, and its insurance
admini strator, Near North Insurance Brokerage, have recommended that the County establish this
allowance within the construction manager's contract.
The funding req uired wi ll be allocated from the New Cook County Hospital contingency.

CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
DOROTHY BROWN, Clerk of the Circuit Court
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Business Management
Consultants, Orland Park, Illinois, to provide consulting, project management, and technical related
services to the C lerk of the Circuit Court. The project involves consolidating the workload on the Clerk
of the C ircuit Court mainframe with Cook County's mainframe. The contractor will assess the support
processes used by the Clerk 's Office and synchronize with the processes of the Department for
Management of Information Systems organization. Processes will include change control, operations
support, and disaster recovery.

3482

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 200 I

Reason:

Business Management Consultants has significant experience in managing data center
consolidations. The company has knowledge of mainframe operating environments similar
to that of the Clerk of the C ircuit Court.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $320,000.00. Contract period: December I, 2001 through November 30, 2002.
(335-260 Account). Requisition No. 2335000 I.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried.

Commissioner Moran voted "present".

respectfully submit to your Honorable Body and recommend for adoption, an ordi nance revis ing the
speed limit o n Lehigh Avenue between East Lake A venue and Chestnut Aven ue, which are under the
maintenance and jurisdiction of Cook County .

with the provisions of Article VI of the Illinois Vehicle Code and as more full y explained in the following
ordinance.

ordinance be adopted.

01-0-27
ORDINANCE

statutory ve hicular speed limits established by Secti on 11 -60 I of the Illinois Vehicle Code are g reater, or
less, than that considered reasonable and proper on the road listed below for which the County has
maintenance responsibi lity and which is not under the jurisdi ction of the Department of Trans portatio n,
State of Illinois; and

investigation upon the road listed below; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED that by virtue of Section 11-604 of the above Code, this Board
detennines and declares that reasonable and proper absolute maxi mum speed limits upon the road

JUDICIAL ADVISORY COUNCIL
CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated September 28, 200 I from
JAMES M. O'ROURKE, Executive Director, Judicial Advisory Counc il
request ing authorization for the Purchasing Agent to e nter into a three year contract with Juvenile Support
Services, Inc. (JSS, Inc.), Chicago, lllinois, to seek Medicaid reimbursement for Cook County for the
costs of health care services provided juveniles detained in the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center
(JTDC). JSS, Inc. will work o n a straight contingent bas is paid only upon recovery of Medicaid
reimbursements to Cook County.
JSS, Inc. has conducted a six-week feasibility study at the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center, a copy
of whi ch has been s ubmitted, and estimates that $15 million can be recovered from Medicaid for its initial
claim within s ix months of Board approval.
JSS, Inc. has unique qualifications to perform this work as they have successfully obtained Medicaid
reimbursement for a number of municipal and county governm ents, as well as the State of Illinoi s. They
have also developed programs w here none previously existed.

3503

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 2001

During the three year proposed contract period, Cook County would reimburse JSS, Inc. a percentage of
funds paid to Cook County at a rate of 12% in year one (November 200 I to October 2002); I 0% in the
second year (November 2002 to October 2003); and 8% for the third year (November 2003 to October
2004). JSS, Inc. proposes to make a one-time retroactive reimbursement claim at a rate of 15%
(November 2000 to October 200 I). JSS, Inc. will absorb all costs associated with obtaining the
reimbursement.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Revenue generating: $15,000,000.00. Contract period: November 1,
2001 through October 31, 2004. Public Safety Fund: 1100. Requisition No. 12050012.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 2001

The office evaluated the responses based on various criteria. The criteria included, but was not limited to:


Can the system accommodate add itional detailed account information?



Does the system provide an audit tra il for all transactions?



Is yo ur company certified as a Minority-owned Business Enterprise (MBE) or Woman-owned
Business Enterprise (WBE)?



Does the system provide security for posting, viewing, and reporting?



Provide the ability to drill down to transaction source?



Environmentally and strategically compatible with the Treasurer' s Office current technical
environment?



Ability to interface with other fi nancial systems?

Based on the results of the office' s evaluation, and the fact that Cook County is currently utilizing J.D.
Edwards software in various offices, J.D. Edwards has been selected to provide the above.
Estimated Fiscal Impact : not to exceed $275,000.00. Contract period: November I , 200 1 through
October 3 1, 2002. (7 17/060-579 Account). Requisition No. I 0600 I 00.
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this req uest.

245573

OFF ICE OF THE COUNTY TREASURER by Michael J. Shine, Chief Deputy Treasurer,
transmitting a Comm unication:
requesting authorization for the Purchas ing Agent to enter into a contract with ASTON
GROUP, Chicago, Illinois, to provide Microsoft Great Plai ns e-Enterprise General Ledger
Accounting Software.
The office prepared and distributed a Request for Proposal (RFP) for General Ledger
Accounting Software in May 200 I. Six potential vendors received a copy of the RFP. The
following four (4) responses were received:
I . Epicor Software Corporation
2. Aston Group (Navis ion)
3. Aston Group (Microsoft Great Plains)
4, Mitchell Humphrey
The office evaluated the responses based on various criteria. The criteria included, but was
not limited to:








Can the system accommodate additional detailed account information?
Does the system provide an audit trai I for all transactions?
Is your company certified as a Minority-owned Bus iness Enterprise (MBE) or
Woman-owned Bus iness Enterprise (WBE)?
Does the system provide security for posting, viewing, and reporting?
Provide the ability to drill down to transaction source?
Environmentally and strateg ically compatible with the Treasurer's Office current
technical environment?
Ability to interface with other financial systems?

3570

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 200 I

Based on the results of the office's evaluation, Aston Group (M icrosoft Great Pla ins) ranked
higher than the other firm s responding.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $323,000.00. Contract period: September 1, 2001 through August
31 , 2002. (717/060-579 Account). Requisition No. I 0600084.

be received and filed.

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Construction of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice
o n Wednesday, October IO, 200 1 at the hour of 10:30 A .M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County
Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items and upon adopti on of thi s report, the
recommendations are as follows:
246725

OFFICE OF CAPITA L PLANN ING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Com munication, dated September 19, 2001 :
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request to enter into a professional services
contract with ALVORD, BURDIC K & HOWSON, L.L.C. in the amount of $ 175,000.00
for engineering services for the Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County Com munity Water
Supply Upgrade.
This project's objective is to upg rade Oak Forest Hospital 's (OFH) 50 year old water supply
system to comply with the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency's community water
supply standards. The upg rade work will be determined by perform ing an engineering
eva luation of the system including the Halsted pump station, 60 utility vaults, OFH pump
station, and a ll OFH reservoirs .
Phase I will include an assessment of the pumping, vault controls and sto rage components of
the distribution system. Phase II will include design services necessary to repair and/or
replace components in the current water supply system.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $ 175,000.00. Bond Issue (33000 Account).
Sufficient fund s have been appropriated to cover this request.
*Referred to the Construction Committee on 10/4/01.

3580

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 2001

Commissioner Hansen asked the total cost of the project.
Michael LaMont stated that the total budget for the project is $1.7 million.
Commissioner Sutker asked what were the deficiencies in the water supply system?
Michael LaMont stated that the deficient areas are the pump supply system and the e lectrical power at the
Halsted Street Pumping Station where there is only a single source of electrical supply. He further
commented that the proposed professional services contract includes the installation of a backup
generator.
Chairman Carr asked Michael Wong, representative of A lvord, Burdick & Howson, L.L.C. to add to
Michael LaMont's statements.
Michael Wong, stated that the current water supply system does not meet current regulations as they
relate to venting requirements, overflow, and tank repairs. Additionally, there is tank painting and some
items that pertain to the pump faci lities which are functional but need to be brought up to current
regulations. Mr. Wong concluded by saying that some of the pumps need to be brought up to current
regulations.
Commissioner Sutker asked when did the !EPA issue its report?
Michael Wong responded that he was not certain but believes it was earlier this year which is the reason
the request for a proposal was developed.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner
Communication No. 246725. The motion carried.
246726

Moreno,

moved

the

approval

of

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated September 19, 200 I:
Transmitted herew ith for your approval is a request to enter into a professional services
contract w ith SOODAN & ASSOCIATES in the amount of $20,000.00 for consulting
services for inspection and reporting services for exterior wal ls and enclosures for various
County buildings.
This County must undergo this inspection in order to comply with City of Chicago Ordinance
req uirements.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $20,000.00. Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 10/4/01.
Commi ssioner Moran asked why the $20,000.00 was not included in the request under Communication
246727.

358 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 200 I

Michael LaMont stated that the $20,000.00 request is to prepare an annual inspection report for all the
buildings located in the City of Chicago which is required by the City of Chicago's Building Ordinance.
The inspection is a visual inspection on the exterior facade of the buildings. He said the Office of Capital
Planning and Policy decided not to include this request in Communication 246727 because the annual
inspection goes beyond the County Building. Once the C hicago Building Department issues its report,
the Office of Capital Planning and Policy will be notified of any exterior repairs required. The Office of
Capital Planning and Policy will then come before the County Board requesting to hire a contractor. Each
facility will be handled on a case by case basis. Mr. LaMont further stated that a critical inspection was
performed last year on the County Building and based on that report, the Office of Capital Planning and
Policy is aski ng for permission to prepare speci ficati ons to renovate the entire building.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Vice Chairman Butler, moved the approval of Communication
No. 246726. The motion carried.
246727

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated September 19, 200 I:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request to enter into a professional services
contract with SOODAN & ASSOCIATES for architectural/engineering services for the
County building exterior renovation.
This project is a major restoration of the exterior of the County building. It provides for an
assessment and restoration of the facade and windows on the exterior and light court. The
renovation will include cleaning and tuckpointing the granite, terracotta and support structure
in addition to repair of the windows. This restoration shall be completed with strict
compliance to historical landmark requirements.
It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve this request.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $ 1, 140,000.00. Bond Issue (7000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 10/4/01.
Commissioner Hansen asked Michael LaMont if he could s peak to the committee in regards to the
replacement of the windows in the County Building.
Michael LaMont stated that plans are for the consultant to make an assessment of what needs to be
replaced. He said the infonnation would be given to the Office of Capital Planning and Policy with
options on the window replacement project. He also stated that the $14 million budget would not cover
replacement of all windows.
Commissioner Hansen stated the commissioners need to have assurance that the replacement windows
wi ll be the same as the original windows.
Michael LaMont stated that as far as he knows the windows will not be changed. He also stated that once
the consultant prepares the evaluation, a report will be brought before the committee that will include
recommendations.

3582

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 200 1

Commissioner Hansen asked what is the goal of the Administration regarding the windows?
Michael LaMont stated that the goal of the Office of Capita l Planning and Policy is to take a look at a ll
windows to determine what replacement or renovation needs to be done.
Chairman Carr called on Suresh G. Pinjarkar, Principal/Director of Engineering, Soodan & Associates,
Inc., to answer Commissioner Hansen's question.
In response to Commissioner Hansen's question, Suresh Pinjarkar stated that the windows will be
replaced wi th the same sash windows as a lready in place.
Commissioner Hansen asked if the committee could receive assurance in writing regarding the windows?
Michael LaMont stated that he would get something in writing for the comm issioners.

OLD BUSINESS
Commissioner Hansen asked why the job is not completed at the Department of Corrections for the
twenty-one e levators?
Michael LaMont stated that the project is behind schedule because at the beginning of the job, the
contractor was understaffed but now has additiona l staff.
Commissioner Hansen asked what is the new scheduled completion date?
Michael LaMont stated he believes sometime in late winter.
Commissioner Hansen asked what is the percentage of completion at the Criminal Court Building?
Michael LaMont stated that at the present time the percentage of completion is 0% because the elevators
have not been taken out-of-service. He further commented that there should not be a problem in meeting
the expected completion date of Summer 2002.
Commissioner Hansen asked what is the completion date for the work being done at the Rockwell
Warehouse?
Michae l LaMont stated that the project is also behind schedule because it needed to be rebid. Mr.
LaMont stated that he would get back to the committee with the reason it had to be rebid and also with the
new expected completion date.
Commissioner Hansen asked what is happening with the medical records renovation?
Michael LaMont stated that he will have a solution soon to the medical records storage problem.

Vice Chairman Butler, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved the approval of Communication
No. 246727. The motion carried.
Commissioner Moreno moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Sims.
motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.

245579

VILLAGE OF MATTESON (NO CASH BID REQUEST). Transmitting a Communication,
dated August 9, 200 1 from Deborah Sims, C hairman, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee,
s ubmitting a request from Bruce M. Buyer, Buyer and Rubin, Attorneys at Law:
Re:

No Cash Bid Application
Permanent Index Numbers: 3 1-16-302-007 and 3 1- I 6-302-009

3585

 JOURNA L OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 200 1

This firm represents the Village of Matteson relative to this Application. The purpose of this
letter is to advise yo u of the Village' s desire to continue its participation in the Cook County
No Cash Bid Program . The Village is interested in acquiring the fo llowing parcels in its
community that have delinquent real estate taxes for two or more years, pursuant to 35 ILCS
200/2 1-90. Please accept this request to obtain said properties which are also Iisted on the
submitted Exhibit "A". Said parcels are located in Matteson, Illinois.
PIN 31-16-302-007 ( Parce l I) is located adj acent to property currently owned by the Village.
PIN 3 1-16-302-009 (Parcel 2) is located directly across the street from Parcel I. The parcels
are located within a natural storm water storage area as determined by the Village's official
flood plain map. Some of the property contains wetlands. The purpose for acquiring these
properties is to maintain them in their natural state as storm water retention and to serve as
passive recreation areas for neighboring subdivisions. The Village wi ll develop nature trails
and observation points fo r appreciation of the native prairie, wetland plants and numerous

Ol-R-642
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TED LECHOWICZ, PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
AND JOHN P. DALEY, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, WILLIAM R. MORAN,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR.,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the County Board has learned with sorrow of the death of Clyde L. Choate, whose
career in public service extended over 47 years; and
WH EREAS, Clyde Choate served in the U.S. Anny during World War II and took part in the
invasions of North Africa, Italy , Sicily, France and Germany; and
WHEREAS, on September 5, 1945, C lyde Choate was awarded the Congressional Medal of
Honor, this nation's highest honor, for conspicuous gallantry and extraordinary heroism without regard
for his own personal safety for single-handedly destroy ing an enemy tank on October 25, 1944, in the
wooded hills near Bruyeres, France, under great and vicious fire after it had overru n our own infantry
lines ; and
WH EREAS, Clyde Choate was also cited for bravery in combat for his actions on the Anzio
beachhead in Italy and twice on the battlefields of France, received the Purple Heart, French Fouragere,
Bronze Star, and a Presidential Unit Citation with Oak Leaf Clusters; and
WHEREAS, C lyde Choate served in the lllinoi s House of Representatives for 30 years (from
1947 through 1977), representing the 43rd Di strict, the 50th Di strict, the 58th District, and the 59th
Di strict, and served as Majority Leader during the 74th General Assembly, as Minority Leader during the
77th and 78th General Assemblies, as Majority Whi p during the 71 st and 72nd General Assemblies, and
as Minority Whip during the 69th, 70th. 75th, and 76th General Assemblies; and
WHEREAS, from 1977 through 1994 C lyde Choate also served as Director of External Affairs
for Southern Illinois University at Carbondale; and

359 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 200 I

WH EREAS, in 1988 the State of Illinois honored Clyde Choate by renaming the Anna Mental
Health and Development Center in his honor [the Clyde L. Choate Mental Health and Development
Center was rededicated on June 16, 1995); and

WHEREAS, Clyde Choate was Chairman of the Illinois delegation to the Democratic National
Convention in 1972; and

WHEREAS, Clyde Choate was a member of the Congressional Medal of Honor Society, the
60 I st Tank Destroyer Battalion, Anna American Legion Post #344, Anna Elks Lodge # 1641 , and Anna
Masonic Lodge #520, and a life member of Anna VFW Post #3455; and

WH EREAS, in these difficult times, we should particularly recognize the loss of a patriot and
hero who received the nation's highest honor for extraordinary bravery; and

WH EREAS, Clyde Choate leaves to cherish his memory his wife, Madonna, his daughters,
Elizabeth Wood and Kim Hughey, two grandchildren, Jo hn C lyde William Hughey and Evan Ross
Hughey, hi s brother, Thomas Choate, his s isters, Creta Yates, Dortha Ballance, and Ethel Marie Marlow,
and many other family members and friends; and

WHEREAS, Clyde L. Choate will be missed by all who knew him.

NOW, T HEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
does hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Clyde L. Choate, offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
family in their hour of sorrow and loneliness, for their loss is shared by all members of this body and by
the people of Cook County, and join his family and friends in honoring his memory; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOL YEO, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the fami ly
of Clyde L. Choate as a memorial of hi s many accomplishments and good works and also spread upon the
official proceedings of this Ho norable Body.

Approved and adopted this 18th day of October 200 I.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioner
Attest: DA YID ORR, County C lerk

Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. President Stroger called for a rising vote. The motion carried unanimously.

Ol-R-643
RESOLUTION

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE WILLIAM R. MORAN AND PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, on November I 0, 1775, the Continental Congress meeting in Philadelphia passed a
resolution stating that "two battalions of Marines be raised" for service as landing forces for the fleet; and
WHEREAS, this resolution sponsored by John Adams, established the Continental Marines and marked
the birth date of the United States Marine Corps; and
WHEREAS, serving on land and sea, these first marines distinguished themselves in a number of
important operations, including first amphibious raid into the Bahamas in March 1776 under the
command of Captain (later Major) Samuel Nicholas; and
WHEREAS, Nicholas, the first commissioned officer in the Continental Marines, remained the senior
Marine officer throughout the American Revolution and is considered to be the first Marine
Commandant; and
WHEREAS, the United States Marine Corps was organized as a " Force In Readiness", to fi ght for,
protect and maintain the peace and freedom every one of us des ires; and
WHEREAS, the men and women of the United States Marines have demonstrated a sense of duty,
loyalty, and pride in th is Nation and in their responsibilities as citizens and as Marines; and
WHEREAS, Marine Corps members have consistently served this Nation with valor, courage, and honor
and, in times of war, many have given their li ves in its defense; and
WHEREAS, November 10, 200 1 will be the 226th Anniversary of the United States Marine Corps; and
WHEREAS, it is fitting that we recogni ze and honor all past and present members of the United States
Marine Corps for their dedication, patriotism, and sacrifices in service to this Nation .
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Pres ident and the Cook County Board of
Commissioners does hereby salute the United States Marine Corps for their 226 years of service, and urge
all citizens to express continued support for the Marines and Marine Corps fami lies stationed throughout
the world during this week.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 2001

Approved and adopted this 18th day of October 200 I.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioner
Attest: DAVID ORR, County C lerk

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION

AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the month of October is recognized as Breast Cancer Awareness Month; and
WHEREAS, in the United States, an estimated 192,200 new invasive cases of breast cancer are expected
to occur among women during the year 200 I and about 1,5 00 new cases of breast cancer are expected to
be diagnosed in men; and
WHEREAS, the risk of breast cancer increases with age. The risk is higher in women who have a
personal or fami ly history of breast cancer. Mammography is especially valuable as an early diagnostic
tool because it can identify breast abnormalities that may be cancer at an early stage before physical
symptoms develop. Numerous studies have shown that early detection increases survival and treatment
options; and
WHEREAS, the American Cancer Society recommends that women age 40 and older have an annual
mammogram and annual c linical breast examination by a healthcare professional, and perform monthly
breast self-examination.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and the Members of the Board of
Commissioners, on behalf of the more than five million residents of Cook County, does hereby take this
opportunity to acknowledge Breast Cancer Awareness Month; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body in recognition of Breast Cancer Awareness Month.
A pp roved and adopted this 18th day of October 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, the recent Census data has confirmed that the Hispanic population is now the nation's
largest minority group; and
WHEREAS, lllinois Masonic Medical Center foresaw the rapid increase in the Hi spanic population and
recognized the growing need for suitable health care services for the underserved Hispanic community;
and
WHEREAS, in 1988, Illinois Masonic Medical Center established Hispanocare Incorporated to provide
Hispanics with the option of selecting bilingual physicians as well as bilingual and bicultural auxi liary
health care service providers; and
WHEREAS, today, Hispanocare provides quality and affordab le preventive medicine education in the
Spanish language and is among the leading agencies servicing the health care needs of the Hispanic
community; and
WHEREAS, Hispanocare is sponsored by Illinois Masonic Medical Center and Gottlieb Memorial, and
is comprised of over 200 bilingual/bicultural physicians and health care specialists who come from a
variety of educational and health institutions and also from individual providers; and
WHEREAS, Hispanocare operates w ithout government funding, raising its operational funds th rough
nominal membership fees, provider hospital and funds raised at their annual gala; and
WHEREAS, on November I 0, 200 I, Hispanocare will celebrate its Thirteenth Annual Gala "Nuestro
Compromiso, Our Commitment", with nearly 500 guests at the Chicago Downtown Marriott.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President of the Cook County Board and the
Members of the Board of Commissioners commend Hispanocare Incorporated for working with the
Hispanic community to ensure the highest level of public health in Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Lucy Aquino,
CEO of Hispanocare, as a token of this Honorable Body' s recognition of Hispanocare's dedication and
service to the Hispanic community.

the bench in 1990 at the age of 73 when he went to work in the office of Chicago litigator William J.

unswerving dedication and commitment to his family, to his profession and to the County of Cook.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does

01-R-658
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI,
DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, October 17, 200 I , was observed as "The National Day of Concern A bout Young People and
Gun Violence"; and

3612

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 2001
WHEREAS, thi s important time of reflection served as a national day of observance, providing young
students and adults with an opportunity to reaffirm their commitment to eradicating gun violence in our
schools and communities; and

WHEREAS, on this day, students, adults and elected officials recited and signed pledges against gun
violence; and

WHEREAS, between 1999 and 2000, approximately 20% of the patients treated by the Cook County
Hospital trauma unit were gunshot victims; and

WHEREAS, during this same time period, the trauma unit treated 1,605 gunshot victims; and

WHEREAS, even more alarming is the fact that 52% of the total gunshot victims were between the ages
of 15 and 24; and

WHEREAS, given that the "muzzle velocity" of guns is now significantly higher, gunshot wounds tend to
be much deeper and more severe, even from a single bullet; and

WHEREAS, the organizers and participants in this noble campaign are indeed correct when they note that
individual choices and actions, when multiplied by those of young people throughout the country, will
make a difference''.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf of
the more than five million residents of Cook County, does hereby applaud the life affirming efforts of thi s
important pub Iic safety campaign and urge all Cook County residents to take cognizance of this positive
endeavor.

Approved and adopted this 18th day of October 2001.

.JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

father of seven children; and
WHEREAS, Walter Triche, Sr. was a native of New Orleans, Louisiana and was educated in the Chicago
Public School system. He graduated from Englewood High School where he was identified as "one who
was most likely to succeed"; and
WHEREAS, Walter was a kindhearted and gentle man who created a nurturing environment for his
family and his friends; and
WHEREAS, through the strength of his convictions, Walter was tireless in his fight for a better tomorrow.
He held a di stinguished career as an officer with the Adult Probation Department until his retirement in
1992. He also believed in the power of the ballot and played a significant role in helping elect
Democratic candidates to elective offices; and
WHEREAS, Walter Triche was committed to his faith in God and this faith was manifested daily in his
compassionate spirit; and
WHEREAS, Walter continually affirmed his devotion to his family, his church and his community and
has left a legacy to live one's life to the fullest as he did.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many friends of
Walter James Triche, Sr., and joins them in honoring his memory; and

publisher of the Danish Pioneer, the oldest Danish-American newspaper in the country, and
WHEREAS, Kresten Steffensen, during hi s tenure of leadership of the Danish Pioneer, for more than two
decades, supported and encouraged numerous Dani sh-American activities and organizations, and

Ol -R-661
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN,

JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR.,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS the social blight of domestic violence has continued to burden America into the 21st
Century, turning many homes into places of torment, and
WHEREAS almost one-third of American women murdered each year are killed by their current or
former partners, usua lly a husband, and approximately I million women ann ually report being stalked by
a male offender, and
WHEREAS many innocent children suffer or witness abuse in their homes, which can sadly spawn
legacies of violence in families across America, and
WHEREAS a comprehensive, coordinated approach must shape our strategy to reduce domestic
violence, utili zing the resources of the federal government in partnership with state, county, and
municipal governments, and local community-based agencies to implement tough and effective
mechanisms to respond to reports of domestic violence, and

3616

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR OCTOBER 18, 2001

WHEREAS in recognition of this need, Cook County has responded with specialized units in its judic ia l
system , including offices of the Sheri ff, State's Attorney, C lerk of the Circuit Court, Chief Judge, and the
Judicial Ad visory Council , to work w ith local victims' advocates to make the criminal justice system
more responsive to victims and more retributive to the ir abusers, and
WHEREAS National Domestic Violence Awareness Month provides a special opportunity to emphasize
that domestic violence is a crime, to warn abusers that they will be prosecuted, and to offer victims more
aid and support, now therefore

BE IT RESOLVED, by John H. Stroger, Jr., President of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County,
that the month of October 2001 , is hereby designated as National Domestic Violence Awareness Month,
and all to whom these presents may come are urged to learn more about this national problem and to take
positive action in protecting communities and fa milies from its devastating effects, and

IN WITNESS WHEREOF, we hereunto set our hand th is e ighteenth day of October, in the year of our
Lord two thousand one.
Approved and adopted this 18th day of October 200 I.
JOHN H. STROG ER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Daley , seconded by Commissioner Silvestri , moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
